item_1.episode_type: discovery
item_1.note: Received Hoosier Cargo Express and Robert Cobb's responses to Plaintiff's First Set of Interrogatories and Requests for Production. Key findings:

DEFENSE STRATEGY: Defendant asserts Martin Whitman and Trey Cooper were independent contractors, not employees. Claims no employees, no policies, no training, no investigation conducted.

CRITICAL ADMISSIONS:
- Admits Whitman and Cooper were present as independent contractors on 9/14/23
- Has contract with Menards to deliver goods, but no contract with Whitman/Cooper
- Only has phone numbers for contractors - suggests inadequate vetting
- Rented Ford E350 from Enterprise; both may have driven it
- Conducted NO investigation into incident
- Has no independent knowledge of alleged incident

DOCUMENT PRODUCTION: Minimal - one photograph and redacted insurance DEC page promised

PRIVILEGE CLAIMS: Claims attorney-client privilege over statements taken by insurer (may be challengeable)

GAPS REQUIRING FOLLOW-UP:
1. Nature of relationship with Whitman/Cooper - how selected, paid, supervised
2. Menards contract not produced - may show control requirements
3. Enterprise rental agreement not produced - need to determine authorized drivers, insurance
4. Full insurance policy not produced - only DEC page
5. Robert Cobb's role/authority unclear
6. Name discrepancy: 'Martin Whitman' vs 'Austin Whitman' needs clarification

STRATEGIC IMPLICATIONS: Independent contractor defense is centerpiece. Must establish actual agency through control test, apparent agency, or negligent hiring/supervision. Lack of policies/training supports both IC characterization AND negligence claims.

NEXT STEPS: Demand privilege log, follow up on insurance DEC page, propound second set of interrogatories, subpoena Menards and Enterprise, depose Robert Cobb (30(b)(6) and individual).

item_13.note: Case: Timothy-Ruhl-A-B-9-14-2023
Client: Timothy Ruhl

This is a narrative summary of the November 7, 2025 call relating to the Timothy Ruhl case. The summary was prepared by Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm and sent to Timothy Ruhl via his Filevine project email on November 7, 2025 at 12:48:38 PM (GMT-05:00). The call with Charles A. Walker occurred earlier that day at 12:41 PM (UTC-05:00). The discussion centered on depositions and mediation scheduling, with a plan to locate a key witness and draft an amended complaint.

During the recap, Charles A. Walker informed Aaron Whaley that the discovery response is ready and clarified that they were not trying to mislead about the appropriate person involved; the person identified is Martin, not Austin Whitman. Aaron Whaley indicated a willingness to discuss settlement numbers but stressed that depositions would be necessary if liability is disputed, noting that mediation would be difficult without both parties’ participation. Walker acknowledged that contacting Martin has been challenging and confirmed that they have not yet made contact with him; they are relying on information from Trey Cooper regarding Martin’s presence at the incident. Whaley proposed drafting an amended complaint while attempting to locate Martin, reflecting a collaborative approach to resolving the case. Both parties agreed to reconvene in a week to discuss progress and to potentially schedule depositions for Trey Cooper and others involved.

As for next steps, Charles A. Walker will attempt to locate Martin and confirm his employment status with Who's Your Cargo. Aaron Whaley will draft an amended complaint and use available resources to locate Martin.

Best,
Aaron Whaley

item_54.note: Case: Timothy-Ruhl-Premise-[DOB-148]
Client: Timothy Ruhl

In the matter of Timothy Ruhl v. Hoosier Cargo, et al. (Jefferson 24-CI-005896), the following communications occurred concerning deposition scheduling and a global settlement demand. The client in this matter is Timothy Ruhl.

On April 15, 2025, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email titled “Timothy Ruhl v. Hoosier Cargo, et al. (Jefferson 24-CI-005896)” to Charles Walker and [EMAIL-149], with William Orberson and Allison Wiles also included, and Timothy Ruhl copied via his Filevine project email address [EMAIL-150]. The message was addressed to Allison Wiles at PPOA Law and carried the subject line reflecting the case caption. Koon advised that attached was Plaintiff’s global settlement demand and stated that this would be the easiest method for everyone involved. He provided a Dropbox link for the documents: https://www.dropbox.com/t/B0AZo8uqazDxAEEC. The email closed with Koon’s signature, including The Whaley Law Firm’s address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222) and contact information (Phone: [PHONE-151]; Fax: [PHONE-152]). A standard confidentiality notice followed, indicating the message was intended only for the named recipient and warning against redistribution or disclosure if received in error.

On April 16, 2025, at 10:32 AM, Allison Wiles (Allie Orberson-Wiles) replied. She thanked Bryce for the demand and stated that the firm could not formally respond until they had Mr. Ruhl’s deposition. She requested that Bryce inform them when Mr. Ruhl would be available for his deposition. She invited further discussion if there were questions. The reply included her direct line [PHONE-153]) and office line [PHONE-154]), her email ([EMAIL-155]), and the firm’s office address (716 West Main Street, Suite 300, Louisville, KY 40202). The firm’s standard confidentiality disclaimer followed in the signature block, noting the privileged nature of the communication and instructing the recipient to contact the sender to report an error if the message was received in error.

Earlier, on April 15, 2025, Bryce Koon had also sent a message to the recipients listed above, with the same case caption and subject. That message reiterated the attachment of Plaintiff’s global settlement demand and again pointed to the Dropbox link for access. The body stated that this method would be the easiest for everyone involved and invited questions or discussion if needed. The same signature block for The Whaley Law Firm and the same confidentiality notice appeared at the end of this email as well.

Finally, on April 29, 2025, at 3:10:47 PM, Bryce Koon sent another email to Allie Wiles regarding the same case. He stated that he had spoken with his client about the deposition and that Thursdays appeared to be the best day for Mr. Ruhl’s availability. He proposed the date 06/05/25 and asked how that date sounded for everyone. The email included Koon’s standard firm signature with The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information and address, followed by the same confidentiality disclaimer noting that the message is intended only for the named recipient and advising recipients who received it in error to notify the sender and delete the message.

In sum, the record reflects three principal communications: (1) April 15, 2025, a demand letter and global settlement demand sent with a Dropbox link; (2) April 16, 2025, a response from Allie Orberson-Wiles indicating deposition scheduling is a prerequisite to formal responses; and (3) April 29, 2025, a scheduling note proposing a Thursday deposition and suggesting June 5, 2025 as a proposed deposition date. The communications repeatedly reference deposition scheduling for Timothy Ruhl in the case against Hoosier Cargo, with formal responses contingent upon timely deposition.

item_94.note: In the matter of 7343 Leisure Court, Louisville, KY 40229, Timothy Ruhl and Maureen Abrasevic, the client is Timothy Ruhl. The case note dated September 14, 2023, records correspondence between Jon Strom, General Counsel for Anderson Communities, and Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm regarding a housing issue at the Leisure Court property. The Re line identifies the property and the tenants, Timothy Ruhl and Maureen Abrasevic.

On February 25, 2025, Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Mr. Strom. She clarified that her office represents Mr. Timothy Ruhl for an unrelated matter, but that Mr. Ruhl and Ms. Abrasevic had reached out regarding the housing issue. They had provided photographs the previous day and stated that a ceiling had fallen in November, that the complex had done nothing about the mold or water damage, and that although the ceiling had been patched, there remains moisture in the ceiling and walls. They alleged that multiple units were affected and that several tenants were being forced to move due to the issue. The clients were in the process of moving out and requested that their February rent be refunded and that they not be charged for March. They planned to vacate the property by the end of March, pending a final inspection of their new home, and they expressed concern that the property office would simply find a new tenant without addressing the concerns. They indicated they looked forward to hearing from Mr. Strom once the investigation into the matter was complete. Tuttle provided her contact details at The Whaley Law Firm, including her new email address.

The following day, February 26, 2025, Jon Strom responded to Ms. Tuttle. He stated that he had discussed the matter with Property Management and had reviewed the work order history for the rental unit. Anderson Communities respectfully rejected the demand for February and March rent. He explained that the photos provided appeared to reflect three separate maintenance requests that occurred over several months and were all addressed in a timely manner: a roof leak, an open window that created condensation, and a mold spot discovered behind a piece of furniture. Each issue was addressed within a matter of days after the resident notified Resident Services. Strom noted that the lease includes a mold and mildew addendum outlining the steps to be taken if the resident suspects a mold issue. He also pointed out that the Kentucky Landlord-Tenant Act provides a notice and opportunity-to-cure process that, in his view, has not been followed by the resident. Finally, he invited any attorney representing Mr. Ruhl—who is not a party to the written lease—to contact him to discuss the matter further and indicated he was willing to provide any necessary clarification, though he was unclear as to Whaley Law Firm’s representation in the matter. Strom provided his contact information and office details for follow-up.

She acknowledged that the schedule could be affected by an incoming weather pattern forecast to bring several inches of rain and reaffirmed the team’s commitment to moving forward, with a Monday update anticipated to reflect any weather impacts.

On February 14, 2025, she again confirmed progress: workers were at the home finishing up the setup, electric hookup was planned for Monday, and water/sewer hookup was planned for Tuesday. The Regional Manager was set to meet with the company constructing the deck on Wednesday to go over the plans. She cautioned that the schedule was subject to the incoming weather and promised another update on Monday to assess weekend weather effects and next steps.

By February 18, 2025, Jody provided another status update. She stated that the home was set and siding completed, and that water and sewer were scheduled for setup that day, though she had not yet received confirmation. She warned that there could be a delay due to weather conditions and noted that the ETA for electric hookup had also been impacted by the weather. She added that deck installation would begin at the beginning of the next week and that she would provide another update on Monday afternoon.

Across these communications, the consistent thread was ongoing progress with setting the home, progress on utility hookups, planned deck construction, and weather-related potential delays, all within the context of the Whispering Oaks – Ruhl Home Purchase.

Re: Whispering Oaks - Ruhl Home Purchase

In February 2025, communications concerning the Whispering Oaks - Ruhl Home Purchase were exchanged between The Whaley Law Firm and Flagship Communities REIT regarding client Timothy Ruhl. The messages also reference Tim and Maureen in connection with the purchase and development of the home, and they include standard confidentiality and privilege notices typical of corporate email correspondence.

The first set of messages began on February 11, 2025. At 2:56 PM, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm wrote to Jody B. Gabel of Flagship Communities REIT to thank her for clarifying the current status of the situation. Sarena noted that it had been a pleasure speaking with Jody and that she and her clients, Tim and Maureen, appreciated the update and stress relief the clarification provided. The email included Sarena’s contact information and a note that her email address is sarena@whaleylawfirm.com, along with the firm’s mailing address and phone numbers.

Jody responded later that same day, February 11, 2025, at 2:02 PM. She thanked Sarena for returning the call and explained that the plan was to have the home set on the lot the following day. She stated she would provide an email update on Thursday with the status and urged Sarena to contact her cell or email if there were additional questions.

A further reply from Sarena arrived on February 13, 2025, at 1:42 PM. Her message began with a brief note that “You don’t often get email from sarena@whaleylawfirm.com,” and then she asked Jody for any updates that could be passed along.

That same day, February 13, 2025, at 2:15 PM, Jody sent another update. He explained that, according to the Regional Manager, the home setters were placing the home together by joining the two sections of the doublewide that day. The setters were expected to return the next day to finish any loose ends. They were waiting on an update for water and sewer connections, and the Regional Manager had observed the clients on site and viewing the progress. Jody also noted that the Regional Manager would provide any new information on water/sewer and electric connections the following day.

On February 14, 2025, at 3:23 PM, Jody followed up again. He reported that, after checking with the Regional Manager, the home setters were on site finishing the process of assembling the home—specifically joining the two sections of the doublewide. He stated that electric hookup was scheduled for Monday and water/sewer hookup was scheduled for Tuesday. The Regional Manager was also set to meet with the company responsible for constructing the deck on Wednesday to review the plans. Jody added that the schedule was subject to an incoming weather pattern, including the prediction of several inches of rain, and that the team remained committed to moving forward with the setup. He promised to provide an update on Monday to reflect how the weather over the weekend affected the plan.

The most recent communications occurred on February 18, 2025. At approximately 1:45 PM, Jody informed Sarena that the home was set and the siding had been completed. He stated that water and sewer hookups were scheduled for that day but that he had not yet received confirmation, and there could be a delay due to weather conditions. He also indicated that the ETA for electric hookup had been impacted by the weather, and that he would pass along any updates as they became available.

In the late afternoon of February 18, 2025, at 1:56 PM (13:56:27 -0500), Sarena replied with appreciation for the update and good wishes. She noted the recent severe flooding in the area around the Park over the weekend and expressed hope that the park itself had not been badly affected. She indicated that they looked forward to further updates as the situation progressed.

Throughout these exchanges, the messages from Flagship Communities REIT repeatedly included standard confidentiality and privilege notices, stating that the communication was intended only for the addressees, that the information may be privileged or confidential, and that forwarding or distribution was strictly prohibited. The notices also instructed recipients who were not the intended recipients to return the message and destroy it.

item_208.note: Timothy Ruhl’s case, filed as Timothy-Ruhl-Premise-[DOB-793], centers on Request 13380236 for certified medical records and billing. The client is Timothy Ruhl. Communications regarding this request were exchanged between HealthMark Group and The Whaley Law Firm, represented by Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager.

On August 9, 2024, at 9:28 AM, Sarena Tuttle sent an email to HealthMark Group (HealthMark Group) reporting that their Certified Medical Records & Billing Request had been completed online, but the download did not fulfill the request. She stated that the dates of service requested were [DOB-794] through [DOB-795], yet only dates of service in 2024 were received. The provided records did not include prior visits in 2023, and certified billing was not provided. She asked HealthMark to contact their office to discuss the matter in further detail and noted that she had attached the original request and the provided documents for reference. Her message included her contact information and reminded that this is The Whaley Law Firm’s new email address for correspondence.

Later that day, at approximately 3:28 PM, HealthMark Group replied via Cortney Wyatt, stating that they had submitted the request ID 13380236 for reprocessing of the medical records indicated in the email. They noted that, according to the processor, there were currently no billing records available in the patient’s chart and asked for patience while the medical records were reprocessed.

Earlier correspondence from Sarena on August 9, 2024 had reiterated the same concerns: the notification indicated the records and billing had been processed, but the actual delivery was incomplete. She again requested dates of service [DOB-796] through [DOB-797], highlighted that only 2024 dates were received, and pointed out that prior visits in 2023 were not included. She reaffirmed that certified billing was not provided and requested contact to discuss the matter further. She attached the original request and the documents for reference and again provided her contact details, including her note that the email address to reach her had changed to Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.

On August 12, 2024, Sarena Whaley of Whaley Law Firm received an automated notification from Baptist Health EFT Server regarding the Timothy Ruhl case. The message, addressed to Sarena at Sarena@whaleylawfirm.com, invited her to access a shared folder named “Ruhl, Timothy 288220818.” The invitation notes that if this is her first time accessing Baptist Health’s EFT site, she will need to set up a password for her account, and she should use the email address to which this message was sent as her username. The invitation to view the shared folder will expire if not verified within 30 days of receipt, and she is instructed to use the “View Folder” link to verify access and view the shared files. The sender’s message read simply: “Ruhl, T 288220818.”

This is an automated message. The email requests that any support issues or questions be responded to via email, and notes that support responses may take up to five business days. Recipients are advised to direct any questions regarding the information shared to the Baptist Health department that originally contacted them. There is a link to a Frequently Asked Questions resource for further information on accessing files from Baptist Health EFT, labeled “Baptist Health EFT FAQs.”

The transmission also includes a confidentiality and privilege notice. It states that the information may be privileged, confidential, and/or exempt from disclosure under applicable law, and that if you are not the intended recipient, you should delete the message and that any disclosure, copying, distribution, or use of the information is strictly prohibited. It further emphasizes that Baptist Health will never request account or personal information via public email or pop-up windows. The notice explains that the email and any attached files are confidential and proprietary and intended only for the named recipients; if you are the intended recipient, further disclosures are prohibited without proper authorization. If you are not the intended recipient, any disclosure, copying, printing, or use is strictly prohibited and may violate federal or state law. If you have received this information in error, you are asked to notify Baptist Health immediately at [PHONE-941] or via email to the sender.

item_283.note: Case: Timothy-Ruhl-Premise-[DOB-1064]. Client: Timothy Ruhl.

Initial client contact on July 22, 2024, with Justin regarding intake for Timothy Ruhl. During the call, Mr. Ruhl stated that he previously had an attorney and currently possesses his case file. The prior attorney told him it was a good case, but he does not have staff beyond the attorney and his wife (who is also an attorney), nor does he have funding to continue with the case expenses.

Mr. Ruhl described an incident that occurred on September 14, 2023, in the parking lot of his apartment complex, where he was physically assaulted by a delivery truck driver. The driver, employed by Enterprise and delivering on behalf of Menards, blocked Mr. Ruhl’s vehicle and refused to move it. After Mr. Ruhl asked the driver to relocate, the driver called him a racial slur and an insult, then struck Mr. Ruhl’s parked vehicle. Mr. Ruhl asked the driver for a business card; in response, the driver, apparently aggravated, exited the truck and punched him in the face. There was also another person in the truck, a passenger—an older Black man—who got out, approached Mr. Ruhl, punched him, and slammed his head to the ground, an act witnessed by Mr. Ruhl’s girlfriend. As a result, Mr. Ruhl sustained head lacerations and back pain. He stated that he has a PR. He also went to the hospital after the incident and noted that he is a smaller, disabled person.

Intake documents were sent via VineSign.

Person Making Contact: Justin
Date & Time: July 22, 2024
